ST. PETERSBURG, Nov. 30.â The most alarming indication
of the spread of the disaffection in the army, extending even to
regiments near the person of th"c Emperor, was given in the airiest
at Tsarskoe-Selo to-day of a number of: soldiers belonging to. the
Yellow Cuirassiers of the Guard, the Hussars of the Guard; and the
Life Guard Riflemen, for presenting a series of petitions,' including
one against the use of* troops for police purposes.
The regiments in question are those which have been 1 especially
selected by General Trepoff to guard the Emperor and his family.
They have been counted upon as being loyal to the last, ready even
. to be torn to pieces in defense of his Majesty, like the. Swiss Guards
of Louis XVI. The arrest, although not for. open sedition, shows
how the leaven of discontent is working even within the. precincts
of the imperial guards at Tsarskoe-Selb. â¢
; The incident. gave rise to. most alarming rumors; in -St. :Peters
burg, including one to the effect thaf the Emperor actually had been

â¢ himself, but the press is assured by a member of the imperial en

DECLARE CHINESE
BOYCOTT IS GROWING
Pacific .Coast Merchants
Mourn Falling Off of
Celestial Trade.
The wholesale shippers of the Pacific
Coast are complaining everywhere that
the boycott on American goods in China
has not been abandoned by. the Chinese,
as has been reported, but is growing
stronger as the months advance. They
declare that the fault does not lie with
the merchants of the Orient, who are
anxious enough to sell American goods,
but with the people of China themselves.
They say that their representatives in
China ports write that the determined
spirit to boycott American goods has be
come so prevalent in China that it has
spread to every class, even the lowest.
M. Thomson, a prominent flour whole
saler and exporter of Seattle, who is at
the Palace on a business trip, said yes
terday that the exportation of flour from
America to China had decreased GO per
cent since the boycott began. Instead of
dying out. he says, the antagonism to
American goods is increasing.
The Pacific Coast merchants have, how
ever, prospered tremendously since the
peace agreement betwen Russia and Ja
pan was signed. One Northern firm has
sent 220.000 barrels of flour into Vladi
vostok since peace was declared. Other
lines of goods have fared equally as well.
According to the reports of the exporters
an unprecedented shipment of goods has
been made from San Francisco to Russia
and Japan during the last two months.
Merchants say Russia is looking more and
more to the United States for her sup
plies.
RAILROAD CONTRACTOR
IS NOT A MURDERER
Heart Disease, Instead of
Blow, Cause of Laborer's
Death.
Special Dispatch to The Call.
TACOMA. Nov. 30. â Martin Welch,
a railroad contractor . on Turn Again
Arm. was discharged by Commissioner
Goodall to-day at the close of a pre
liminary hearing- at Seward, Alaska,
to determine the measure of his- re
sponsibility for the death of August
Nllson, a laborer. In his camp 'ln 'an
altercation on October 19. The Com
missioner found, as did the Coroner's
jury he Impaneled the day after , the
tragedy, that Nilson died of heart dis
ease. All the doctors testified that
Nllson's heart was !n such a state that
he was liable to drop dead at . any
moment. This entirely 'clears, Welch,
who had slapped Nilson Just before he
dropped dead.

CZAR BAL.KS DE WITTE.
.\ew Premier- Already, Practically'
\u25a0'\u25a0:\u25a0; Shorn ot His Power:
BERLIN; Nov. 30.â The St. "Peters
burg correspondent of the ' Vosslsche
Zeitung, Who talked for five hours with
representative leaders of all political
and social classes outside the ' court
circle, cabled by way 'of Stockholm un
der yesterday evening's date as fol
lows: 7;:::;. ;^ r
"The results of .these interviews is
the conclusion that the action of " the
Zemstvo Congress in recognizing the
Socialistic organization as the strong
est has driven many wavering elements
to join the Socialists, although these
openly proclaim that the capitalists
will be abolished as soon as tne Gov
ernment is displaced. A rich merchant
informed me that, he pays $50 weekly
to the strike" leaders, "who give him a
permanent guard of workmen.
"Confidence in Premier de Witte's
Cabinet is disappearing in political and
commercial' circles, since it is growing
dally more evident that Do Witte. is
without the necessary powers from the
Emperor.. These circles believe right
ly that General Count Ignatieff's influ
ence is growing. \u25a0\u25a0'"'-'â¢
"Partisans of the reactionary Interior
Minister Durnovo confirmed to me the
statement that Prince Tcherbatoff is
organizing a loyal militia and addod
that Durnovo and Tcherbatoff "were
trying to force matters to such an ex
treme that at- a t given' moment tney
can fall upon the Liberals with'thfs
temporary militia.' These classes des
ignate Durnovo as De Witte's successor.
In a very few days a crisis must de
cide whether the autocracy will ; "be
resurrected. vâ¢ ; ; .
"The Socialists are very optimistic.
They hope soon; to spread. a ; general
strike throughout Russia, except; ln Po
land. They regard all the technical
troops as pledged to them. Of the
other troops. they do not yet trust the
division of guards.
"The Socialists say. that 'the. activity
of the reactionists /comes -very, oppor
tunely for them, since "it drives the
Liberals jto the Socialists.; which facil-;
Jtates 'their fight against the capital
ists. They assert, that, they have no
doubt that the proletariat will, be su
preme "In St. Petersburg within aivery
short time, although only part of the
lower officials of the post and telegraph
departments ' have hitherto joined ; the
strike. The railroad operatives ."also
will strike, soon, because Durnovo/ ar
nested their representatives contrary to
the Government's promis6.
"In some Quarters there is a demand
for ; the \u25a0 Emperor to come to St. Peters
burg and' Issue a manifesto to the
peaceable, elements.- It seems to me
that the moment for this has, passed.
The Emperor's \ entrance .Into -.the' city
could only \u25a0 lead ;to a. : catastrophe which
may be postponed'or. perhaps; be avoid
ed by his remaining at. TsarskoerSelo.
"According to my. personal .convic
tion the situation: grows vhourly^ worse.
Events cannot Jbe - stayed and new
bloodshed ; is .unavoidable^ since . the re
actionists and : Socialists' alike .wish It.
The Imperial: house and the bourgeois
will be the losers." . -

Leah Captures. Two Races at the Polo Association Meet
".* Rudolph Spreckels'- thoroughbred

Many interesting tournament tennis
matches were played yesterday on t'.vs
courts. At Claremont Herbert Schmidt
and Harry Rolf e won the first annual
scratch doubles tournament , for the
three-time- challenge cups offered by th-?
club. At the park Mtss Gfolda Myer and
George Janes carried off the honors In
the handicap mixed doubles tournament.
The "draw" doubles event at the Califor
nia Club was won by Harold Gabriel and
E. H. Vogel.
The most important event was the
doubles across the bay. In the finals
the Baker brothers, one of the strongest
teams at the park, .were opposed \u25a0 to
Schmidt and Rolfe, probably the beat
team of the California Club. Both team*
were at their best and Â«on* htgh-cla*"
tennis was played. Schmidt and Rolfe
lost the first set by a narrow margin,
but w.on the next three. ( '
The Bakers played their "usual careful,
steady game and it proved effective In
the opening set. This was the closest
set of the four. The Bakers did -sorny
clever lobbing and as usual made very
few errors. In the remaining sets RolfÂ«
and Schmidt also steadied down and
their errors Wearne less numerous. The
score was C-3.* 6-4. K-4. "5-3.

teresting matches. . In the finals Miss
Myer and Janes won rather easily from
Miss Hotchkiss and Griffin. The former
received, owe odds of 3-6 and won in
straight ~sets.
